class="cl-9a3edfe8">Mozambique;Zambia;Botswana</span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4"> </span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4">initiated</span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4"> </span><span class="cl-9a3edfe8">cooperation</span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4"> </span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4">toward</span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4"> </span><span class="cl-9a3edfe8">Zimbabwe</span><span class="cl-9a3edfe8">Revolutionary</span><span class="cl-9a3edfe8"> </span><span class="cl-9a3edfe8">Army</span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4">.</span></p></td></tr><tr style="overflow-wrap:break-word;"><td class="cl-9a3f2ce6"><p class="cl-9a3eebfa"><span class="cl-9a3edfd4">307.4</span></p></td><td class="cl-9a3f2cdd"><p class="cl-9a3eebfa"><span class="cl-9a3edfd4">On 13 April 1979 Rhodesian forces captured 14 people in Francistown, Botswana, which had been occupied by ZAPU, destroying the ferry between Botswana and Zambia, allegedly used for supplies to ZIPRA. Clashes between Rhodesian and Mozambiquean forces, the latter better equipped than those of Botswana, were frequent in 1979.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9a3f2cdd"><p class="cl-9a3eebfa"><span class="cl-9a3edfe8">Rhodesia</span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4"> </span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4">initiated</span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4"> </span><span class="cl-9a3edfe8">battle/clash</span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4"> </span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4">toward</span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4"> </span><span class="cl-9a3edfe8">Mozambique</span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4">.</span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4"> </span><span class="cl-9a3edfe8">Rhodesia</span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4"> </span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4">initiated</span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4"> </span><span targets.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9a3f2cdc"><p class="cl-9a3eebfa"><span class="cl-9a3edfe8">Zimbabwe</span><span class="cl-9a3edfe8"> </span><span class="cl-9a3edfe8">People’s</span><span class="cl-9a3eebfa"><span class="cl-9a3edfd4">307.6</span></p></td><td class="cl-9a3f2cdd"><p class="cl-9a3eebfa"><span class="cl-9a3edfd4">Some of the more serious recorded attacks took place on 9-10 February, on the Mapai-Pafuri road; on 20 February, on the Chimoio guerrilla base; the 14 March bombing of Chokene; and the 18-21 April bombings of Mozambique army positions in the Gaza Province.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9a3f2cdd"><p class="cl-9a3eebfa"><span class="cl-9a3edfe8">Zimbabwe</span><span class="cl-9a3edfe8"> </span><span class="cl-9a3edfe8">People’s</span><span class="cl-9a3edfe8"> </span><span class="cl-9a3edfe8">Revolutionary</span><span class="cl-9a3edfe8"> </span><span class="cl-9a3edfe8">Army</span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4"> </span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4">initiated</span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4"> </span><span class="cl-9a3edfe8">attack</span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4"> </span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4">toward</span><span class="cl-9a3f2cdc"><p class="cl-9a3eebfa"><span class="cl-9a3edfe8">Rhodesia</span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4"> </span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4">initiated</span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4"> </span><span in 1979, on 26 June, 1 and 20 July, 23 August, and throughout the month of October.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9a3f2cdd"><p class="cl-9a3eebfa"><span class="cl-9a3edfd4">No</span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4">307.9</span></p></td><td class="cl-9a3f2cdc"><p class="cl-9a3eebfa"><span class="cl-9a3edfd4">After the elections in Rhodesia in April 1979 a new government led by Bishop Abel Muzorewa took office on 31 May. Muzorewa quickly made it clear that his government intended to continue the policy of preemptive attacks on guerrilla bases and economic targets in Botswana, Mozambique, and Zambia.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9a3f2cdc"><p class="cl-9a3eebfa"><span class="cl-9a3edfe8">Rhodesia</span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4"> </span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4">initiated</span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4"> </span><span with reports of about 1,000 people being killed each month.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9a3f2cdd"><p class="cl-9a3eebfa"><span class="cl-9a3edfe8">Zimbabwe</span><span class="cl-9a3edfe8"> </span><span class="cl-9a3edfe8">Rhodesia</span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4"> </span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4">initiated</span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4"> </span><span 12,000.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9a3f2cdc"><p class="cl-9a3eebfa"><span class="cl-9a3edfd4">No</span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4"> </span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4">events.</span></p></td></tr><tr forthcoming as long as the government and constitutional structure of Muzorewa's Zimbabwe-Rhodesia remained unchanged.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9a3f2cdd"><p class="cl-9a3eebfa"><span class="cl-9a3edfd4">toward</span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4"> </span><span class="cl-9a3edfe8">Zimbabwe</span><span class="cl-9a3edfe8"> </span><span class="cl-9a3edfe8">African</span><span class="cl-9a3edfe8">People’s</span><span class="cl-9a3edfe8"> </span><span class="cl-9a3edfe8">Revolutionary</span><span class="cl-9a3edfe8"> </span><span class="cl-9a3edfe8">Army;Zimbabwe</span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4"> </span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4">initiated</span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4"> </span><span class="cl-9a3edfe8">meeting</span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4"> </span><span class="cl-9a3f2ce6"><p class="cl-9a3eebfa"><span class="cl-9a3edfd4">307.30</span></p></td><td class="cl-9a3f2cdd"><p class="cl-9a3eebfa"><span class="cl-9a3edfd4">Lord Carrington played a very strong role in the negotiation process, often dictating the pace and substance of the talks.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9a3f2cdd"><p class="cl-9a3eebfa"><span class="cl-9a3edfe8">United</span><span class="cl-9a3f2cdc"><p class="cl-9a3eebfa"><span class="cl-9a3edfd4">Specifically, he used the possibility of recognition and an end of sanctions as an incentive to Muzorewa and as a threat to the PF. By 15 November some progress had been made at Lancaster House: agreement on transitional arrangements for Rhodesia had been reached; and the British government had proposed the establishment of a Cease-Fire Commission on which military commanders of both sides would be represented.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9a3f2cdc"><p class="cl-9a3eebfa"><span class="cl-9a3edfd4">No</span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4">307.32</span></p></td><td class="cl-9a3f2cdd"><p class="cl-9a3eebfa"><span class="cl-9a3edfd4">Despite apparent political progress, Rhodesia expanded its economic pressure on Zambia with a series of major military attacks.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9a3f2cdd"><p class="cl-9a3eebfa"><span class="cl-9a3edfe8">Rhodesia</span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4"> </span><span class="cl-9a3eebfa"><span class="cl-9a3edfd4">307.33</span></p></td><td class="cl-9a3f2cdc"><p class="cl-9a3eebfa"><span class="cl-9a3edfd4">A crisis for Zambia was triggered on 17 November when Rhodesian forces attacked a bridge on the main road to Tanzania; Zambian villagers were killed, and another vital bridge linking Zambia to Malawi and Mozambique was blown up.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9a3f2cdc"><p class="cl-9a3eebfa"><span class="cl-9a3edfe8">Zambia</span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4"> </span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4">experienced</span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4"> </span><span </span><span class="cl-9a3edfe8">crisis</span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4"> </span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4">about</span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4"> </span><span class="cl-9a3edfe8">act</span><span canceling all military leaves, and announcing a call-up of reserves.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9a3f2cdd"><p class="cl-9a3eebfa"><span class="cl-9a3edfe8">Zambia</span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4"> </span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4">initiated</span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4"> </span><span class="cl-9a3edfe8">raise</span><span class="cl-9a3edfe8"> </span><span class="cl-9a3edfe8">in</span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4">307.35</span></p></td><td class="cl-9a3f2cdc"><p class="cl-9a3eebfa"><span class="cl-9a3edfd4">On 12 December Lord Soames, newly appointed Governor of Rhodesia for the interim period, arrived in Salisbury to oversee the cease-fire, elections, and the transfer of government.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9a3f2cdc"><p class="cl-9a3eebfa"><span December.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9a3f2cdd"><p class="cl-9a3eebfa"><span class="cl-9a3edfe8">Mozambique;Botswana</span><span class="cl-9a3edfd4"> </span><span traced to the era of Spain's colonial rule.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9a643f72"><p class="cl-9a640f48"><span class="cl-9a64043a">No</span><span class="cl-9a64043a"> </span><span class="cl-9a95da8c">315.1</span></p></td><td class="cl-9a961506"><p class="cl-9a95e54a"><span class="cl-9a95da8c">Poland, the USSR, Czechoslovakia, and East Germany were enmeshed in another major intra-Soviet-bloc upheaval from 14 August 1980 to 13 December 1981.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9a961506"><p class="cl-9a95e54a"><span class="cl-9a95da8c">No</span><span class="cl-9a95da8c"> </span><span class="cl-9a95da8c">events.</span></p></td></tr><tr style="overflow-wrap:break-word;"><td class="cl-9a96151a"><p class="cl-9a95e54a"><span class="cl-9a95da8c">315.2</span></p></td><td class="cl-9a96151b"><p class="cl-9a95e54a"><span class="cl-9a95da8c">BackgroundSince the formation of Poland's Communist regime in 1944 there had been several violent outbursts of internal discontent, notably in 1970 and 1976, which led to major changes in both the party and state leadership.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9a96151b"><p class="cl-9a95e54a"><span class="cl-9a95da8c">No</span><span class="cl-9a95da8c"> </span><span class="cl-9a95da8c">events.</span></p></td></tr><tr style="overflow-wrap:break-word;"><td class="cl-9a961510"><p class="cl-9a95e54a"><span class="cl-9a95da8c">315.3</span></p></td><td class="cl-9a961506"><p class="cl-9a95e54a"><span class="cl-9a95da8c">In the summer of 1980, too, a wave of industrial unrest gripped Poland in response to marked increases in food prices.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9a961506"><p class="cl-9a95e54a"><span class="cl-9a95da8c">No</span><span class="cl-9a95da8c"> </span><span class="cl-9a95da8c">events.</span></p></td></tr><tr style="overflow-wrap:break-word;"><td class="cl-9a96151a"><p class="cl-9a95e54a"><span class="cl-9a95da8c">315.4</span></p></td><td class="cl-9a96151b"><p class="cl-9a95e54a"><span class="cl-9a95da8c">However, violence was conspicuously absent from strikes and demonstrations led by Solidarity, an independent trade union headed by Lech Walesa, later the first President of Poland in the post-communist era.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9a96151b"><p class="cl-9a95e54a"><span class="cl-9a95da8c">No</span><span class="cl-9a95da8c"> </span><span class="cl-9a95da8c">events.</span></p></td></tr><tr style="overflow-wrap:break-word;"><td class="cl-9a961510"><p class="cl-9a95e54a"><span class="cl-9a95da8c">315.5</span></p></td><td class="cl-9a961506"><p class="cl-9a95e54a"><span class="cl-9a95da8c">Yet for the Soviet Union, as for the U.S. in the Americas, unrest anywhere in Eastern Europe was perceived as a risk to Moscow's hegemony.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9a961506"><p class="cl-9a95e54a"><span class="cl-9a95da8c">No</span><span class="cl-9a95da8c"> </span><span class="cl-9a95da8c">events.</span></p></td></tr><tr class="cl-9a95da8c">This concern had already given rise to the Brezhnev Doctrine, during the Prague Spring crisis in 1968: this asserted the concept of limited sovereignty among members of the bloc and the Soviet Union's right to intervene in the domestic affairs of any member when bloc interests -- as defined by Moscow -- were threatened by internal events.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9a96151b"><p class="cl-9a95e54a"><span class="cl-9a95da8c">No</span><span class="cl-9a95da8c"> </span><span class="cl-9a95da8c">events.</span></p></td></tr><tr class="cl-9a95da8c">On 14 August 1980, 17,000 Polish workers at the Lenin shipyard in Gdansk went on strike and occupied the huge industrial complex.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9a961506"><p class="cl-9a95e54a"><span class="cl-9a95daa0">Poland</span><span class="cl-9a95da8c"> </span><span class="cl-9a95da8c">initiated</span><span class="cl-9a95da8c"> </span><span Poland.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9a96151b"><p class="cl-9a95e54a"><span class="cl-9a95da8c">No</span><span class="cl-9a95da8c"> </span><span class="cl-9a95da8c">events.</span></p></td></tr><tr Walesa, was arrested.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9a961506"><p class="cl-9a95e54a"><span class="cl-9a95daa0">Poland</span><span class="cl-9a95da8c"> </span><span August.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9a9e6eea"><p class="cl-9a9e42da"><span class="cl-9a9e3808">Malta</span><span class="cl-9a9e37f4"> </span><span class="cl-9a9e37f4">initiated</span><span of endangering peace in the Mediterranean.</span></p></td><td class="cl-9a9e6eea"><p class="cl-9a9e42da"><span class="cl-9a9e37f4">No</span><span class="cl-9a9e37f4"> </span><span
